  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_72e32f1c-88cf-4f22-9f8f-7f0245ca8080'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer199864061206840640">Ceony Twill arrives at the cottage of Magician Emery Thane with a broken heart. Having graduated at the top of her class from the Tagis Praff School for the Magically Inclined, Ceony is assigned an apprenticeship in paper magic despite her dreams of bespelling metal. And once she’s bonded to paper, that will be her only magic…forever.<br/><br/>Yet the spells Ceony learns under the s</span>
  <span id="freeText199864061206840640" style="display:none">Ceony Twill arrives at the cottage of Magician Emery Thane with a broken heart. Having graduated at the top of her class from the Tagis Praff School for the Magically Inclined, Ceony is assigned an apprenticeship in paper magic despite her dreams of bespelling metal. And once she’s bonded to paper, that will be her only magic…forever.<br /><br />Yet the spells Ceony learns under the strange yet kind Thane turn out to be more marvelous than she could have ever imagined—animating paper creatures, bringing stories to life via ghostly images, even reading fortunes. But as she discovers these wonders, Ceony also learns of the extraordinary dangers of forbidden magic.<br /><br />An Excisioner—a practitioner of dark, flesh magic—invades the cottage and rips Thane’s heart from his chest. To save her teacher’s life, Ceony must face the evil magician and embark on an unbelievable adventure that will take her into the chambers of Thane’s still-beating heart—and reveal the very soul of the man.<br /><br />From the imaginative mind of debut author Charlie N. Holmberg, <i>The Paper Magician</i> is an extraordinary adventure both dark and whimsical that will delight readers of all ages.</span>
  <a data-text-id="199864061206840640" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">As this series seems to be set in an era somewhere between the Victorian and the 20's , the romance element is more....wholesome. There are a few kiss<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">As this series seems to be set in an era somewhere between the Victorian and the 20's , the romance element is more....wholesome. There are a few kisses and one thought of the heroine "wishing he were less a gentleman and more a rogue" (which honestly made me snicker). The whole series was a delightful spin on a gentler age with more "light" magic than "dark".<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1023917025" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12177202439087124846">Have you ever had someone try to tell you a story. Because they are excited you get excited and can't wait to hear it! But they are speaking so fast that they are leaving out important details which makes it impossible to follow the story. So you politely nod your head and pretend to listen even though you are zoning out and thinking of other things... Did I bring in all the groceries? What was the name of my high school math teacher? At the same time your friend really wants to emphasize her st</span>
  <span id="freeText12177202439087124846" style="display:none">Have you ever had someone try to tell you a story. Because they are excited you get excited and can't wait to hear it! But they are speaking so fast that they are leaving out important details which makes it impossible to follow the story. So you politely nod your head and pretend to listen even though you are zoning out and thinking of other things... Did I bring in all the groceries? What was the name of my high school math teacher? At the same time your friend really wants to emphasize her story so she repeats the same things over and over which seriously doesn't help and try as you might you still can't piece together what she is saying. In the end you just continue nodding and thinking soon the story will come to an end and you can make your get away. <br /><br />Sent from my iPad</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1103753802" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1103753802" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1103753802?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1103753802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7242005710387154338"><blockquote>
  <i>“One more,” she promised herself. “One more until the end. And even if there’s no door to freedom, at least you know you tried. One more, Ceony.”</i>
</blockquote>This was a good book. At the beginning, I was getting solid heavy magical Daddy Long Legs feels...which descended solidly into Dickensian feels, more specifically, <i>A Christmas Carol.</i> Then it became nigh unbearable, because <b>constant flashbacks are not for me, no, sir.</b> Excellent premise. A heroine that I liked. It was just a shame that this turned out</span>
  <span id="freeText7242005710387154338" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“One more,” she promised herself. “One more until the end. And even if there’s no door to freedom, at least you know you tried. One more, Ceony.”</i>
</blockquote>This was a good book. At the beginning, I was getting solid heavy magical Daddy Long Legs feels...which descended solidly into Dickensian feels, more specifically, <i>A Christmas Carol.</i> Then it became nigh unbearable, because <b>constant flashbacks are not for me, no, sir.</b> Excellent premise. A heroine that I liked. It was just a shame that this turned out to be such a boring book for the latter 2/3s.<br /><br />The good: light on the romance, the heroine is genuinely likeable, no Mary Sues here, the main character gave me heavy Snape feels (without the greasy hair), and the romance...oh, so very light.<br /><br />Not to mention I seriously want to take up origami now.<br /><br /><u>The Summary:</u><blockquote>
  <i>Every window in the mansion—and Ceony counted only seven—hid behind black shutters all chained and locked, without the slightest glimmer of candlelight behind them. Dead leaves from a dozen past winters clogged the eaves and wedged themselves under bent and warped shingles—also black—and something drip-drip-dripped nearby, smelling like vinegar and sweat.<br /><br />The tiles composing the path up to the front door, which hung only by its top hinge, were cracked into pieces and overturned, and Ceony didn’t trust a single one of the porch’s gray, weathered boards to hold her weight long enough for her to ring the bell.<br />“I’ve been shot to hell,” Ceony murmured.</i>
</blockquote>A most inauspicious beginning to young magician <b>Ceony</b>'s apprenticeship. In this alternate reality of England, there exists magic. There exists magicians. Each magician, once graduated, is assigned a speciality.<br /><br />Ceony has been given paper, or as they call it, <b>folding</b>.<blockquote>
  <i>Her heart had broken at those words, and now, standing before the gate of Magician Emery Thane’s lair, she wished it had stopped beating altogether.<br /><br />Mg. Aviosky obviously did not realize that the reason Folding had become a dying art was because the skills it enabled were so completely useless.</i>
</blockquote>Paper. The seemingly most useless of all the magical arts. What can you possibly do with paper?<br /><br />And what's worse...Ceony is sent off into the backwaters of England, into a dank, dingy old home...<blockquote>
  <i>A skeleton greeted her.<br /><br />The eyeless head of the skeleton looked up and down almost mechanically, and Ceony, with a hand over her heart, realized all six feet of it was comprised of paper—its head, its spine, its ribs, its legs. Hundreds, perhaps thousands of pieces of paper, all white, rolled and Folded and pinched together to connect in a variety of joints.</i>
</blockquote>If this is the reception, <b>what could the owner possibly be like?</b><blockquote>
  <i>“He’s mad,” Ceony said, aloud this time.</i>
</blockquote>Well, not really. <b>Magister Thane</b> is quite average. Really.<blockquote>
  <i>He seemed quite average, his skin neither light nor dark, his height neither short nor tall, and his build neither thin nor broad. His dark hair fell just below his ears in a sort of kempt-but-unkempt way. He had black sideburns down to his jaw, and his nose had a slight bump to it, just above the middle of the bridge. The only thing extraordinary about him was the brightness of his eyes—green as summer leaves and shining as if someone had hid a light behind his forehead.</i>
</blockquote>Magister Thane may not be mad, but he is <b>immensely eccentric</b>, as we readers love for our magicians living in the wilds of England to be. His magic lies in paper, and his entire house is decked out in paper.<br /><br />And like any bachelor magician, he doesn't know how to cook, and he doesn't have two beans in his cabinet. Try as she might, Ceony can't help but pity the guy, but there is no doubt to the fact that he is brilliant at what he does. Ceony wanted a teacher, she's got one.<blockquote>
  <i>His hands stilled, revealing a stout fish between them, puffed out in the middle to form a three-dimensional body. Folds similar to the orange bird’s wings formed its pectoral fins. Mg. Thane picked it up, whispered to it, and released it. The fish soared upward through the air as a real fish would in water, its tail fin paddling back and forth until it hit the ceiling—which Ceony noticed had been covered with long pieces of white paper tied together with a simple string. The white fish used its puckering mouth to bite down on the string and untie its looping knot.</i>
</blockquote>And like any good, mysterious magician...he's got something to hide.<blockquote>
  <i>She lowered the fortuity box and narrowed her eyes at him. “Who’s Lira?”<br />Mg. Thane’s expression did not waver, nor did his stance, but for a moment Ceony could have sworn his eyes flickered dark and back. Only . . . no, they weren’t quite as bright as before. Perhaps it was the late-growing sun outside the library window, but she didn’t think so.</i>
</blockquote>Life is quiet. There is a lot to learn, and Ceony's days are consumed with books...and cleaning. It is a terribly old house, after all. It is a peaceful existence until <b>the day that woman shows up</b> and does <b>something unthinkable.</b> In a single moment, Ceony's world is overturned...and she has two choices. Run away, or face what she fears, despite her greenness, despite her status as an amateur folder. Does Ceony stand a single chance against one who is so much stronger, one who works the dark art of <b>Excision?</b> She must.<blockquote>
  <i>The snowflake still felt frosty, just like real snow. Snow he had made for her. All of it had been for her in one way or another, hadn’t it?<br />In the glow of the candlelight she said, “I have to do it. I have to save him.”<br />For she knew no one else would.</i>
</blockquote><u>Ceony</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>Ceony had the feeling that, should she get to the buggy with Mg. Aviosky now, she’d run away and never come back. And, though she despised it, Ceony knew she needed to wait for her new responsibility to settle before she could trust herself near any easy exits. She had bound herself to paper indefinitely, and it did her no good to push through a year at Tagis Praff just to throw it all away now.</i>
</blockquote><b>Ceony is a very likeable, approachable character.</b> She is not overtly feminine. She is intelligent...she had to have been, to have graduated from her school so quickly, at the top of her class, but that doesn't mean she is 100% mature. Quite the contrary at times.<blockquote>
  <i>“Well, the absence is rude, isn’t it?” Ceony asked, hating how childish the words sounded in her mouth. She cleared her throat and sucked in a deep breath. “I’m sorry. I’m a little on edge.”</i>
</blockquote>She has a rather grim sense of humor, but above all else, Ceony has practicality. She didn't get the fate she chose, but she never dwells upon the unfairness of it. She makes the best of her circumstances.<blockquote>
  <i>Ceony couldn’t bond paper and still hope to be a Smelter, enchanting jewelry and bespelling bullets as she had often daydreamed during her lessons.<br />It wasn’t fair, but there was no use in further complaining.</i>
</blockquote>She is brave, but never a martyr.<br /><br /><u>Final comments</u>: It was a solid book, but besides the fact that I found it dull, this book was missing a lot of spark, a lot of soul. I liked all the characters. The love interest was sweet, and there was very, very little romance. This book just lacked that special quality that made the things and the characters within it come to life within my imagination.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7242005710387154338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15091914532629168757">I give up. I tried I really did. DNF'd at 51%..I just can not make myself continue. I always feel bad when I don't finish a book but this one just has not captured my interest in the least. <br/><br/>The premise is good. </a><br/><br/><i>I receive</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15091914532629168757" style="display:none">I give up. I tried I really did. DNF'd at 51%..I just can not make myself continue. I always feel bad when I don't finish a book but this one just has not captured my interest in the least. <br><br>The premise is good. The story however, just bobbles along and I'm soooooo pooped from reading it that I want to smash small china doll heads into the wall.<br>I don't care for the main characters..don't care for the story..just don't care..STOP judging me!<br><br>The only part I liked was the paper folding.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/QYwi0qe" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417915081ra/12595902.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>I received an arc copy of this book from Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>

<div id="review_1019693903" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1019693903" />
    <a title="Melanti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3034846-melanti"><img alt="Melanti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286146966p2/3034846.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1019693903?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanti" href="/user/show/3034846-melanti">Melanti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22521286-the-paper-magician">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3034846-melanti?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3034846-melanti?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3034846-melanti?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3034846-melanti?shelf=kindle-lendable">kindle-lendable</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1019693903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13462504462747310628">I'm pretty picky about my historical fiction. I want it to be, well, historical. If it's set in the early 1900's, I don't want the characters to use modern slang, like something being "shot to hell." I want them to talk and relate to each other as people of the period did. Granted, it does make it tricky for the authors sometimes - to make characters that fit in with historical social conventions but that are still appealing to contemporary audiences. If all you do is take characters who talk an</span>
  <span id="freeText13462504462747310628" style="display:none">I'm pretty picky about my historical fiction. I want it to be, well, historical. If it's set in the early 1900's, I don't want the characters to use modern slang, like something being "shot to hell." I want them to talk and relate to each other as people of the period did. Granted, it does make it tricky for the authors sometimes - to make characters that fit in with historical social conventions but that are still appealing to contemporary audiences. If all you do is take characters who talk and act as if they were in contemporary times and dress them in period garments and give them candles instead of light bulbs... Well, that's something I'm always going to be a bit disappointed in. Why even bother? It's like you've set your book at a costume party!<br /><br />I guess Steampunk has made the era popular, but there's so much a modern setting could have done for this book! If Paper Magicians were out of style because electronic media were taking over - emails over printed letters, ebooks over physical books - wouldn't that just be awesome and interesting? <br /><br />Could there be magicians aligned to circuit boards? Or would magicians for plastic and smelting have to work together? <br /><br />Instead, we're just told that Folding has gone out of style and we're left to assume that's because it's mostly used for decorative and entertainment purposes... Yet we're not really told what can be done with the other materials. <br /><br />It's a shame really. This book could have been so wonderful. It's got such a whimsical premise that I immediately picked it out of the Kindle First selections this month without even looking at the other options, but in reality, most of that whimsy is left unexplored.<br /><br />Perhaps my expectations were too high? Maybe the cover art had me subconsciously expecting another <i>Jonathan Strange and Mr. Norrell</i> (which this certainly isn't) or maybe the typically masculine author name didn't leave me prepared enough for the level of romance in the book.<br /><br />And sadly, the romance doesn't appeal to me at all. In part that's because I'm not a big fan of romances to begin with, but the romance in this book is particularly unappealing to me because it's all about the GUY. The relationship starts out as a student/teacher relationship, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and he's PAID for her education so there's some extra weight to the student/teacher status as well <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> so it's an extremely unequal scenario from the very start. But then <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[about a third to half the book is the main character getting a cliff notes summary of the love interest's past - so  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> she gets to know HIS past really well, but neither the reader nor the love interest gets to know her at even close to the same level of detail. It's very one-sided. And after reading the book, I glanced at the author's bio and saw this about her relationship with her husband: "Shortly afterwards, her darling husband dragged her to Moscow, Idaho, where he subsequently impregnated her." Granted, it's a joke to some extent... But I can't help but notice that sentence is all about the guy too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13462504462747310628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1017873790" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1017873790" />
    <a title="Caroline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3530786-caroline"><img alt="Caroline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574167910p2/3530786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1017873790?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline" href="/user/show/3530786-caroline">Caroline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1017873790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11980965974521441649">This book honestly has A LOT of promise. The writing isn't bad, even if there were many times I didn't feel the author was true to time period or location. The subject matter was interesting and I liked the idea of the world of magic being split this way, bonding to a specific medium. It was also interesting that the world of magic was generally an accepted part of life in this realm of reality. But there were some big flaws I couldn't overlook, including a desperately dragging second half that </span>
  <span id="freeText11980965974521441649" style="display:none">This book honestly has A LOT of promise. The writing isn't bad, even if there were many times I didn't feel the author was true to time period or location. The subject matter was interesting and I liked the idea of the world of magic being split this way, bonding to a specific medium. It was also interesting that the world of magic was generally an accepted part of life in this realm of reality. But there were some big flaws I couldn't overlook, including a desperately dragging second half that felt as though it were written as a plea for a screen play rather than a novel.<br /><br /> **SPOILERS BELOW**<br /><br />However, what started out as a promising, fascinating book devolved for me when the second half of the book was spent nearly entirely in visions that didn't even belong to the lead character. I didn't understand the logic of bringing the dog on the rescue journey. I think this would have been more powerful or useful to me if this segment of the book had been no more than a third of the book, either with more descriptions of magical life and relationship development in the beginning, or application of the lessons and visions from inside the heart and on the journey to life after the adventure. All in all, there was just way too much time spent on the section in the heart and everything that followed felt rushed, cliched, and predicable in a way that did not utilize effectively anything I'd learned in the trudge through the rescue. I spent the whole second half wishing the book would just move on and get back to the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11980965974521441649" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2118528466" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2118528466" />
    <a title="Maria V. Snyder" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1629797-maria-v-snyder"><img alt="Maria V. Snyder" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530814046p2/1629797.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2118528466?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria V. Snyder" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria V. Snyder" href="/user/show/1629797-maria-v-snyder">Maria V. Snyder</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2118528466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11365414283018186819">I really enjoyed this book. The magical system in the book and series, is very unique as magicians bond to certain man-made materials like paper, glass, steel, etc... and once bonded they can use them. For example the main protagonist, Ceony can make a paper bird and it will then "come to life" and she can use it to scout for danger or find a person.<br/><br/>The setting is England around Victorian times, but doesn't have that "woman can't do [fill in the blank]" vibe. Ceony is very likable and the story </span>
  <span id="freeText11365414283018186819" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book. The magical system in the book and series, is very unique as magicians bond to certain man-made materials like paper, glass, steel, etc... and once bonded they can use them. For example the main protagonist, Ceony can make a paper bird and it will then "come to life" and she can use it to scout for danger or find a person.<br /><br />The setting is England around Victorian times, but doesn't have that "woman can't do [fill in the blank]" vibe. Ceony is very likable and the story took an unexpected turn, going in a direction I didn't predict (a good thing!). There were just a few places where my suspension of disbelief was stretched, but minor quibbles all. I enjoyed the interaction between Ceony and Emrey--another character who I liked just as much.<br /><br />This book made me look at paper in an entirely different light! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11365414283018186819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1981843314" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1981843314" />
    <a title="Lauren (Shakespeare &amp; Whisky)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32342930-lauren-shakespeare-whisky"><img alt="Lauren (Shakespeare &amp; Whisky)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490838820p2/32342930.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1981843314?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren (Shakespeare &amp; Whisky)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren (Shakespeare &amp; Whisky)" href="/user/show/32342930-lauren-shakespeare-whisky">Lauren (Shakespeare &amp; Whisky)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32342930-lauren-shakespeare-whisky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32342930-lauren-shakespeare-whisky?shelf=self-published">self-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32342930-lauren-shakespeare-whisky?shelf=1-and-2-star-books">1-and-2-star-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1981843314" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13330394149265113256"><i>
  <b>"For the past five years, Ceony had wanted to be a Smelter. However, while most graduates… got to choose what material they dedicated their craft to, Ceony had been assigned."</b>
</i><br/><br/>This book was very, very frustrating. <br/><br/><i>Have you ever read a book and wished another author would steal the premise and write a much better book?</i> <br/><br/>The premise was fascinating, original and clever. A recent graduate of the Tagis Praff School for the Magically Inclined, Ceony had her heart set on becoming a smelter. You can </span>
  <span id="freeText13330394149265113256" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"For the past five years, Ceony had wanted to be a Smelter. However, while most graduates… got to choose what material they dedicated their craft to, Ceony had been assigned."</b>
</i><br /><br />This book was very, very frustrating. <br /><br /><i>Have you ever read a book and wished another author would steal the premise and write a much better book?</i> <br /><br />The premise was fascinating, original and clever. A recent graduate of the Tagis Praff School for the Magically Inclined, Ceony had her heart set on becoming a smelter. You can only magically bond with one material and after your bonding ceremony that material is the only one you can work. <br /><br />Ceony, a scholarship student with a perfect memory, is assigned to paper. An ignoble and unglamorous specialty. Her teacher is strange and possibly mad. <br /><br />What a great premise! A victorian- era, light- hearted, well mannered romance. An action adventure where Ceony uncovers a dark conspiracy of blood workers (a dark and dangerous magic). Dark pasts, brooding love interests. AWESOME…<br /> <br />Yeah… not so much. The writing can be really clunky, the love interest develops without any real effort at charisma or even much interaction. And pretty early on stuff gets… weird. Basically, Ceony gets trapped in her teachers heart and travels through his memories. <br /><br />Why create a great world with cool magic and then have the bulk of the story stagnant in a weird dream sequence? Ceony hadn't learnt enough! Not enough had happened in the real world. Her relationship with her teacher had not grown to the degree that what she did made any sense. It was too easy, too weird and too convenient. And it was all over way to fast. It pissed me off. <br /><br /><b>This novel was such a disappointment. Made more bitter by the glimmers of incredible potential.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13330394149265113256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1058771826" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1058771826" />
    <a title="Doug Warren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2135772-doug-warren"><img alt="Doug Warren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403893396p2/2135772.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1058771826?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doug Warren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doug Warren" href="/user/show/2135772-doug-warren">Doug Warren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1058771826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7180611016998785743">A note before I start the review. If the author ever happens to read this, or anyone considering writing a book based in a different time or place--just saying it is set in England at the turn of the 20th Century doesn't make it so. It is very hard to get into it when everything sounds like modern day language and dialogue. It sounds exactly how people speak today. Even when the story told me the year and the place, I had a hard time feeling it. Read D. H. Lawrence's <i>Sons and Lovers</i>. That's how </span>
  <span id="freeText7180611016998785743" style="display:none">A note before I start the review. If the author ever happens to read this, or anyone considering writing a book based in a different time or place--just saying it is set in England at the turn of the 20th Century doesn't make it so. It is very hard to get into it when everything sounds like modern day language and dialogue. It sounds exactly how people speak today. Even when the story told me the year and the place, I had a hard time feeling it. Read D. H. Lawrence's <i>Sons and Lovers</i>. That's how this book needs to feel. That's how the dialogue needs to sound. If not, your book will never be believable. Honestly, if this book had been set in present day America, and had a lot of the unneeded details and adjectives cut out, it would have been better. Would have definitely garnered more stars than me. But as it is, well, you'll see my opinion in my review. My apologies up front, because I'm going to be a bit of a jerk. <br /><br />Now, on to the review:<br /><br />Boooooooo! Booooooooooo! I don't think I have ever booed a book in a review before, but this one was more than deserving. I've had Amazon Prime for a while, but August was the first month I remembered to get one of the free ebooks, and boy, I can tell ya, what a let down. I mean, wow, the author sure can put a lot of words on paper without saying anything. And some of her similes and metaphors are just laughable--unnecessary and distracting. And I guess this book is set in England...because everyone once in a while it has some attempt at using an English term, word or colloquialism, but since it is not constant, it just makes it awkward. So, prediction 1-this author is American, and probably had never visited the UK. Prediction 2-she was homeschooled as a child, or grew up Mormon, or something else that keeps you out of the real world, shelters you...something. I mean, is undergarments too big of a swear word to say that we have to call them underthings...And the book is about magicians, and she makes note of one of them noticing the other didn't pray before a meal...well, pretty sure in any realm practicing sorcerers aren't Christians (or followers any other Abrahamic religion)...so they wouldn't pray before a meal, right? And, I mean who else besides a right-winged American would describe an English girl right out of school traveling with a gun in her suitcase? (When I wrote this I hadn't figure out it was set around 1900 yet. Now it makes more sense, but come on! A reader shouldn't be surprised by the year come page 60 or so!) But she describes currency as pounds, so it has to be the UK, right? But the whole ambiance of the book is American. You can't just say a few British words and phrases and call it good. Just like how saying you saw a yearbook from 1888 doesn't all of a sudden make the book feel like it's taking place 100 years ago. That's not how setting works. And I get it, I know, I know, I am not the target demographic for this book. But having been a language arts and reading teacher the past five years, I know there is good stuff out for preteens/young adults. There is quality work. To put this book out and give it to them because they might enjoy it because they don't know any better is insulting. I have read books that were boring, but I could appreciate and give a good review because of the mastery of the word play. And then there are books that I absolutely love with zero literary value, but they are just so darn entertaining. But this book had no redeeming qualities. I hate this book more than Roger Ebert hated any of Rob Schneider's movies. Even with the review as it is so far, I think I am painting it in more of a positive light than I really feel it deserves. I would rather hold in a really uncomfortable fart for 3 hours in a room full of people I look up to and respect and would be humiliated if I embarrassed myself in front of them than have to spend 3 hours reading this steaming pile again. I mean, I have read owners' manuals for lawn mowers that were more entertaining than this. I have read a lot of self published books, and of course they are amateurish; they are amateur books! But this one looks like it is coming from a real publisher, and it is more amateur and poorly written than anything self published, barring the worst of the worst. The only thing this book has going for it over self published stuff is it seems to be free of typos. So yay for the proof reading! BUT! When you were proof reading, for the love of Vishnu why didn't you revise it!?! It's like my 4th graders in class. When I tell them it's time to edit and revise, oh they do the editing well, putting in periods and commas and making sure everything that needs to be capitalized is, but the revising is where they get messed up. They are married to their work and don't want to erase anything. So when there is crap, instead of taking it out, they pile more crap on top of if. And then they get a steaming pile of crap. Like <i>The Paper Magician</i>. The more I read the worse it got. She went up stairs and smelled mildew and it was cooler than down stairs. Before there was air conditioning? That's not how attics work. That's how basements work! This is why you need to proofread for more than just punctuation and grammar mistakes! <br /><br />Oh. To any future readers of this book-- once you get to the "exciting" part where she is in that thing (don't want to say what for spoilers sake, but it's the main thing you aren't going to miss it) skip to the last chapter. Yep. It's horribly boring and takes way too long to say what is happening, but in the last chapter she gives an abridged version of what happened in a conversation. So yeah. Those tedious chapters were all a waste because you find out what happened without them. <br /><br />In other words, don't buy this book. Don't read it. The only reason I read it all is because after the first few pages I knew I had to write this review, and I wanted it to be as honest as possible. If the book had just one redeeming quality, I would have told you. But it didn't. I have never hated a book as much as this one. Booooooooo! Booooooooooooo!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7180611016998785743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1045285305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1045285305" />
    <a title="rubywednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5896025-rubywednesday"><img alt="rubywednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311804522p2/5896025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1045285305?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="rubywednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="rubywednesday" href="/user/show/5896025-rubywednesday">rubywednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5896025-rubywednesday?shelf=ya-supernatural">ya-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5896025-rubywednesday?shelf=don-t-waste-your-time-money">don-t-waste-your-time-money</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5896025-rubywednesday?shelf=ya-historical">ya-historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5896025-rubywednesday?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5896025-rubywednesday?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1045285305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2206979384564986704">I was trying to think of what was wrong with this book and the only thing I could come up with is that is too wishy-washy. When all the details, from the magic rules to the setting to the time to the characterisation, are as so vague it's impossible to get invested in a book.<br/><br/>First up, the positives. The imagery was pretty and impressive. The first third or so of the book had all these cool paper things coming to life and it was so nice. It had a similar quality to The Night Circus. It had the gu</span>
  <span id="freeText2206979384564986704" style="display:none">I was trying to think of what was wrong with this book and the only thing I could come up with is that is too wishy-washy. When all the details, from the magic rules to the setting to the time to the characterisation, are as so vague it's impossible to get invested in a book.<br /><br />First up, the positives. The imagery was pretty and impressive. The first third or so of the book had all these cool paper things coming to life and it was so nice. It had a similar quality to The Night Circus. It had the guts of a good concept and I was intrigued at first. <br /><br />Um, that's all I've got. <br /><br />The rest sucked.<br /><br />First of all, when was this book set? Someone please tell me because the text sure didn't make it clear. It seemed to be some alternate version of London in the early part of the last century. Plastic's been available for thirty years. They ride in buggies. They dress in older. idek. Culturally, other than a mention of the Thames, it didn't resembled any London I'm familiar with. Makeup was only recently popular, too. <br /><br />The main character was bratty and then silly and then just blah. You can tell the author was really trying to make her independent and strong. That was cool, I guess. She was always cooking for the guy. Like at least fifty meals were described. At least forty nine of them didn't fit with what people of their apparent class/background would be eating in the past. Rice and pasta and even sausage gravy and biscuits (!!) were not on the menu then. She was meant to be an apprentice but she spent more time doing her boss/future love interests laundry and cooking. <br /><br />yay! feminism! The romance here represented a particular kind of relationship that you see a lot in certain books and I was super uncomfortable with it. So, she was only 19 and she developed a crush on her boss/master. It seemed to be her first time even spending time with a guy tbh. As the book progresses, they fall in love in about two days, she still cooks and cleans, risks her life to save him from his evil ex wife, and sees a vision where they will grow old together and have kids. Oh, we also find out he saw her working at an event when she was much younger and decided to fund her magic education. <br /><br />So every aspect of her life revolves around him. I mean, that's just so creepy and paternalistic and ugh. <br /><br />The plot was lame. The rescue wasn't nearly as exciting as you would think. it involved literally wandering around his stolen heart. yeah<br /><br />I guess this is meant to be a YA book. Even though the main characters are 19 and 30ish. It reads young and not in a good way. Honestly, it was kind of insulting.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2206979384564986704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2425411002" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2425411002" />
    <a title="R.K. Gold" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40737518-r-k-gold"><img alt="R.K. Gold" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518717825p2/40737518.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2425411002?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R.K. Gold" class="user" itemprop="url" name="R.K. Gold" href="/user/show/40737518-r-k-gold">R.K. Gold</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22521286-the-paper-magician">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2425411002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12072825297600434262">At the moment I'm saying 3 but it's possibly 3.5<br/><br/>As usual, my reviews contain spoilers so if that bothers you stop reading now.<br/><br/>So, I wasn't bored reading this book but it did leave me questioning the point of it all. Let me begin this by saying I think it was an interesting concept, I have faith it is going to be an entertaining series, and the writing was fine. That being said, it was a short book and a substantial amount of it took place through sort of flashbacks. What I mean is they weren't f</span>
  <span id="freeText12072825297600434262" style="display:none">At the moment I'm saying 3 but it's possibly 3.5<br /><br />As usual, my reviews contain spoilers so if that bothers you stop reading now.<br /><br />So, I wasn't bored reading this book but it did leave me questioning the point of it all. Let me begin this by saying I think it was an interesting concept, I have faith it is going to be an entertaining series, and the writing was fine. That being said, it was a short book and a substantial amount of it took place through sort of flashbacks. What I mean is they weren't flashback scenes but during the climax of the story Ceony is pursuing an excisioner (and her teacher's former love interest) to rescue Emery's heart.<br /><br />Of course, it's a bit of a play on meaning since Ceony is also in love/starting to fall in love with her teacher and is willing to go to great lengths to rescue him from his past. I thought the world itself has potential as does the magic system but we barely see any of that. We know Ceony was familiar with the magical world and the non-magical world so it wasn't like Harry Potter, the two worlds are integrated. <br /><br />The story is really only two parts. There's the first portion where Ceony is learning how to be a folder, and the second part when a dark magician bursts through the door, takes Emery's heart, and Ceony pursues. We learned far more about Emery than we do about Ceony. Though Ceony tries to hold her own with Emery's troubled past by listing every mistake she made in life, it didn't paint nearly as whole of a picture as the scene by scene journey through Emery's life.<br /><br />As I said, I was entertained enough to continue this series and I see a lot of potential upside, but nothing about this book blew me away. That being said, the series might end up being fantastic since all my complaints are of omission and not faults in the book itself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12072825297600434262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9043114581777724844" style="display:none"><b> Full Review </b><br /><br />Liked the beginning and the end, but the middle was sloooow<br /><br /><b> What I liked </b><br />- I liked the unique concept of the story. Before reading, I thought ‘The Paper Magician’ was some sort of metaphor but it’s actually about a magician that can manipulate paper. It may seem boring (and the MC thought that at first) but the manipulations were actually quite interesting. There are also other magical affinities such as fire, glass and metal. There is also the dark affinity which is the manipulation of flesh. This book mostly focused on the paper and flesh affinities. I also liked how people aren't born with a magical power, but they get to choose and bond with one.<br /><br />- I loved the relationship!!! There wasn’t any romance in this but it is hinted and I shipped them!! It has a forbidden angle (Teacher and Student, a big age gap: 19 and 30, which just made me ship them even more lol. I just love how they did things for each other before any romance was even hinted at. This is slow-burn/friendship first type of situation and I loved it!<br /><br /><b> What I didn’t like </b><br />- The middle was so slow: It pretty much involved going down memory lane for a long time and it reminded me of books that have long travelling sections. I just wanted it to be over!! <br /><br />- I didn’t understand/saw the point of some of the things that the villain did in this <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Why did she trap the girl in his heart instead of just killing her??  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, it was okay and I would continue reading the books for 3 reasons: The books are really short, like a little bit over 200 pages, the slow middle seemed like it was unique to this book and thirdly, I want to read about my ship sailing!!!<br /><br /><b> Pre-reading </b><br />I really hope there is romance in this because the last two books I read didn't really have any, which is bad for my romance addiction</span>

</i><br><br><b>Quick review:</b><br><br><u>What I loved:</u><br><br>- The characters. They were funny, peculiar, interesting and very easy to relate to. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390450431ra/8215506.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>- The plot. It never gets old.<br><br>- The writing. Very Dickensian, and it flowed amazingly well. I <i>adored</i> the way the author described things and seemed to give everything a voice... even a paper dog. <br><br><u>What I didn't love:</u><br><br>- The pacing. It was either too slow or too quick. Nothing happened for pages and pages and pages and then everything happened in the space of three chapters. It didn't give me enough time to catch up with what was going on and , sometimes, I had to re-read the page to understand fully what was happening.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383344422ra/6513654.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>- The overly long descriptions. Sometimes, Ceony described something as boring as a tree for over half a page, and I began losing interest. So I skim-read and then, obviously, missed major points, and I had to go back and put up with the description all over again.<br><br><b>Overall:</b><br><br>A very solid three stars! <br><br><b>Full review to come on <a href="http://magazine.100percentrock.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">100% Rock!</a></b><br><br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1771260322624650411">The paper magic was really fun, but literally half the book is spent in someone's memories, which started to drag, and didn't seem to serve much of a purpose besides fostering a one-sided infatuation that I didn't care for much. <br/><br/>Then there's the blood magician threat, which an entire force of magicians and police have been fighting - but <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Ceony doesn't even get questioned seriously about what happened and how she succeeded against a blood magician who had ripped her master's heart </span></span>
  <span id="freeText1771260322624650411" style="display:none">The paper magic was really fun, but literally half the book is spent in someone's memories, which started to drag, and didn't seem to serve much of a purpose besides fostering a one-sided infatuation that I didn't care for much. <br /><br />Then there's the blood magician threat, which an entire force of magicians and police have been fighting - but <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ceony doesn't even get questioned seriously about what happened and how she succeeded against a blood magician who had ripped her master's heart out? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Towards the end, I also began to notice an increase in modern concepts and American words and phrases, when this is supposed to be set in London around the turn of the 20th Century. Needless to say, I found it jarring and irritating.<br /><br />So it sounds like I didn't like this much. But I liked it well enough. The concept of paper magic was really interesting, and I enjoyed all the details of folding. It just had some distracting aspects and was not as developed as I like. I can see why some people are calling it YA even though Ceony is 18 and out of school. There's something too simple about it to be adult. I was hoping for it to be more than it was, that's all. I think I will probably still pick up the sequel at some point.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1106685596" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1106685596" />
    <a title="Kaora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7983564-kaora"><img alt="Kaora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542069606p2/7983564.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1106685596?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaora" href="/user/show/7983564-kaora">Kaora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1106685596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15532327561432492795"><i>How many others had she judged and set aside like that, thinking them no more than a one-sided piece of paper?</i><br/><br/>In The Paper Magician, Ceony, a new graduate of Tagis Praff School for the Magically Inclined she has been forced to study a part of magic no one else will - paper. Upset about not being able to choose to go into the medium of her choice, she is surprised to discover Mg. Thane is nothing like she expected. When he is attacked by a Excisioner, a magician using flesh as a medium, who then </span>
  <span id="freeText15532327561432492795" style="display:none"><i>How many others had she judged and set aside like that, thinking them no more than a one-sided piece of paper?</i><br /><br />In The Paper Magician, Ceony, a new graduate of Tagis Praff School for the Magically Inclined she has been forced to study a part of magic no one else will - paper. Upset about not being able to choose to go into the medium of her choice, she is surprised to discover Mg. Thane is nothing like she expected. When he is attacked by a Excisioner, a magician using flesh as a medium, who then steals his heart it is up to her to save him.<br /><br />I'm hovering between 3 and 4 stars here. I finally settled on 4 because for a first book I was thoroughly impressed. Her writing was simplistic, yet beautiful making this a really enjoyable read. I'm definitely keeping an eye out for some of her later works.<br /><br /><b>Positives</b><br /><br />The main character was not very likeable at the start being bratty and snooping through Mg. Thane's things, but she started to grow on me as she realized that things aren't what she assumed. It was a joy to watch her grow throughout the book. She is headstrong and gets herself into some bad situations. But is smart and resourceful and isn't afraid to speak her mind. I found myself liking her.<br /><br />My favorite character was Mg. Thane, who while a tad eccentric, did his best to be kind to Ceony even when she didn't deserve it. <br /><br />The world was well built. At no time did it feel like information overload, nor did I feel like I was missing details. It was shown piece by piece in a way that world. And I loved the new take on magic. How magicians manipulated mediums such as paper, rubber, plastic, metal and glass, creating things such as paper flying machines, or bullets that don't miss.<br /><br />The romance was a tad cheesy but I didn't hate it. You heard it here first folks. Kaora found a book where she did not mind the romance! There was no insta-love. Spotting a person across the room and instantly wanting to brush that hair out of their face. There was no love triangle. Because you aren't pretty unless you have two guys fighting for you. Ceony got to know Thane and genuinely started to care about him.<br /><br />The pacing was good for the first half of the book. At no time did I feel bored with it. In fact I read it in its entirety in a day, which is rare for me. I often have to switch between books.<br /><br /><b>Negatives</b><br /><br />I'm going to have to put the romance here too. Mg. Thane was her teacher and he is 31 and she is 19, making it a tad bit on the creepy side.<br /><br />The pacing for the last half of the book was not as great as the first half. It seemed to be a little more rushed. I would have liked to see more on Lira and Mg. Thane. I felt like the author touched on it, but didn't go into too much detail.<br /><br />Overall I am really impressed and I recommend anyone who needs a light and clever fantasy read.<br /><br />Cross posted at <a href="http://www.hisaye.net/paper-magician-charlie-n-holmberg/" rel="nofollow noopener">Kaora's Corner</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15532327561432492795" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1755172140" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1755172140" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1755172140?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kaylin by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/59252392-lexi">Lexi</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1755172140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6612659823541625092"><b> 3 Stars:<br/><br/>Overview: </b><br/><br/>I finished this book 17 days ago and I’m just now actually writing this review…<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475123301ra/20683690.gif' width='500' height='281' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>Oh well, better late than never right?<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14287011.Charlie_Holmberg' title='Charlie Holmberg' rel='nofollow noopener'>Charlie Holmberg</a>'s book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20727654.The_Paper_Magician__The_Paper_Magician_Trilogy___1_' title='The Paper Magician (The Paper Magician Trilogy, #1) by Charlie N. Holmberg' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Paper Magician</a> takes place in a fictionalized Victorian era where magicians are bound to one element—meaning they can only preform magic using that component. The story begins with the reluctant Ceony beginning her apprenticeship in the arts of paper magic, under the care of one Emery Thane.<br/><br/><b> Pros: </b><br/><br/>I love, love, <i>love</i> this idea. Everyth</span>
  <span id="freeText6612659823541625092" style="display:none"><b> 3 Stars:<br><br>Overview: </b><br><br>I finished this book 17 days ago and I’m just now actually writing this review…<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475123301ra/20683690.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Oh well, better late than never right?<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14287011.Charlie_Holmberg" title="Charlie Holmberg" rel="nofollow noopener">Charlie Holmberg</a>'s book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20727654.The_Paper_Magician__The_Paper_Magician_Trilogy___1_" title="The Paper Magician (The Paper Magician Trilogy, #1) by Charlie N. Holmberg" rel="nofollow noopener">The Paper Magician</a> takes place in a fictionalized Victorian era where magicians are bound to one element—meaning they can only preform magic using that component. The story begins with the reluctant Ceony beginning her apprenticeship in the arts of paper magic, under the care of one Emery Thane.<br><br><b> Pros: </b><br><br>I love, love, <i>love</i> this idea. Everything about it. Not only do I think the magical aspect of this is rather unique and very interesting in itself, but I was very excited to learn this doubled as a historical fiction. The time-era really blends with this well.<br><br>Both the main characters are very interesting to me. I was never bombarded with background information or details about their personalities, but I was given enough I had an understanding of them before the plot settled in—and then I was allowed to slowly learn more and more. I thought this was handled quite well, with the appropriate amount of showing versus telling. <br><br>The writing here definitely wasn’t absurdly gorgeous or original, but it also wasn’t stale. It avoided clichés with clever phrasing that I really enjoyed. One of my personal favorites was“Ceony’s skeleton slumped within her skin.” Which seems very odd, but in context allowed for me to perfectly picture Ceony’s reaction. <br><br>I really loved the villain this this. She was coy without being overtly so, and it was great slowly learning more about her <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ both in real time and in flashbacks. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I <i>love</i> how Ceony took out Lira. It wasn’t outright vicious, but it certainly wasn’t tame. It was believable for both their characters and I feel the repercussions of this action are notable throughout the rest of the series.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The thing I was most excited to read about was the different uses for paper-magic. I was not disappointed, this was vastly creative and super entertaining. <br><br>There were several details that I found kind of clever and enjoyed. For instance, Ceony seems to share several characteristics with the element she binds to (paper). She’s scared of water and says it makes he feel as if she will “fall apart.” There were more, but I don’t remember them all right now. I also thought the term Excisior was clever in itself, considering the form of magic they practiced. <br><br><b> Cons: </b><br><br>The main thing that drew me in to this book was this fantastic world full of magic. I couldn’t wait to see how it was structured—how are elements assigned? How do the different magicians work together? What roles do they have in society? Is this magic something everyone has; or a chosen few? And… I never really got to see that. Around 25% in, this book rapidly changes plot-wise, and the rest of the book ends up being very flash-back filled and introspective. This <i>was</i> interesting… but seemed premature. I think it would have worked much better in a sequel. If I’d been given a book to learn more about these characters and this world, this entire plot would have had more impact to me<br><br>Since there <i>was</i> such a rapid plot shift, it’s hard to really talk about what I disliked—as most of it came after. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ To clarify, as my non-spoiler comments are very vague. This whole journey through Thane’s heart and “learning-more-about-him/falling-in-love" would have fit much better in a sequel to me, compared to my introduction to these characters.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I really would have preferred seeing Ceony come into her own and learn to accept working with Paper Magic <i>without</i> love being part of the equation. I certainly wouldn’t have minded her falling in love later on, but I feel the story about her accepting herself and this new life-style should have been separate from that.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I didn’t really pick up on any chemistry between the two-love interests? I honestly thought it was just a friendly relationship until it wasn’t.<br><br>The first 25% (before the plot shift) seemed to drag a little bit. I think Holmberg was trying to build up to this later plot-shift, but until that happened, there really wasn’t a lot plot wise. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Uh… why didn’t Lira just crush/stab his heart once it was out of Thane’s chest? She didn’t seem to have any plans with it, and it would have killed Thane in time anyway, so it’s not as if she wanted him alive. I don’t get it.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><b> In Conclusion: </b><br><br>This went a completely different direction than I was expecting, and I was a little let down by that. But it still held my interests and I’m intrigued to read more of this world.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6612659823541625092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText3854452453375428195" style="display:none">In this story, a magically inclined individual versed in the art of Folding can create 'living' creatures, braided belts that protect and vitalize the body, and even beating hearts - all out of Folded paper. <span id="freeTextContainer2243935388403772252">Mostly, this was just badly paced. I liked the beginning of this SO MUCH. The slow unfolding of the world, Ceony learning about paper, the dynamic between the characters.<br/><br/>But then the plotty stuff happened! And, first of all, I think it happened too quickly. I wasn't invested enough in the world and characters yet. And I didn't think Ceony knew enough yet.<br/><br/>And then the plotty stuff dragged ON AND ON. I was so frustrated with it, but had read enough that I didn't want to DNF it.<br/><br/>And I was all ready </span>
  <span id="freeText2243935388403772252" style="display:none">Mostly, this was just badly paced. I liked the beginning of this SO MUCH. The slow unfolding of the world, Ceony learning about paper, the dynamic between the characters.<br /><br />But then the plotty stuff happened! And, first of all, I think it happened too quickly. I wasn't invested enough in the world and characters yet. And I didn't think Ceony knew enough yet.<br /><br />And then the plotty stuff dragged ON AND ON. I was so frustrated with it, but had read enough that I didn't want to DNF it.<br /><br />And I was all ready to ship the main characters, but . . . not the way it was done.<br /><br />And while I'm usually not one that cares a ton about details, a lot of them here really jarred. Particularly all the references to makeup in the very early 1900's.<br /><br />I'm sort of tempted to read the next one, but I probably shouldn't.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14712577442761509798">DNF 51%<br/><br/>Another book that was just not for me. I honestly try not to make a habit of binning books, however life is too short for bad books and I can only put up with so much. I feel like my lack of enjoyment of this book was my penance for picking a book based on its cover ( which is awesome btw).<br/><br/>I loved the concept but the execution just didn't work for me. The main character was alright but nothing special. I had no real investment to anyone or anything in this story. Hardly anything happened </span>
  <span id="freeText14712577442761509798" style="display:none">DNF 51%<br /><br />Another book that was just not for me. I honestly try not to make a habit of binning books, however life is too short for bad books and I can only put up with so much. I feel like my lack of enjoyment of this book was my penance for picking a book based on its cover ( which is awesome btw).<br /><br />I loved the concept but the execution just didn't work for me. The main character was alright but nothing special. I had no real investment to anyone or anything in this story. Hardly anything happened until 45%ish and even then the action was...lacking.<br /><br />Overall there just wasn't enough happening in this book to warrant the investment of my time.<br /><br /><b> Buy, Borrow or Bin Verdict: Bin</b><br /><br /><br /><br />Note: I received this book for free in exchange for an honest review.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14670607213381085670">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to Amazon Publishing and NetGalley.)<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Material made by man, your creator summons you. Link to me as I link to you through my years until the day I die and become earth.”</i>
