She was rude to her new employer, rude about his house, and whenever given t</span>
  <span id="freeText14670607213381085670" style="display:none">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to Amazon Publishing and NetGalley.)<br><br><b>
  <i>“Material made by man, your creator summons you. Link to me as I link to you through my years until the day I die and become earth.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421336426i/13360831._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>This book started out quite promising, but unfortunately took a big turn for the worse.<br><br>I found Ceony quite a rude person, and she was also really, really nosey! She was rude to her new employer, rude about his house, and whenever given the chance would happily nose around his office and his bedroom, rifling through his things, and generally spying on him!<br><br><b>
  <i>“The front you put on your home is horrid.”<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421336426i/13360832._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>“The tiniest smile teased her lips as she sat down in Mg. Thane’s desk chair and began opening his drawers, none of which had been locked.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421336426i/13360833.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The storyline in this started out okay, I liked the way the magicians made so many things from paper, and did things with it that you maybe wouldn’t think of, like making an origami dog.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Ceony gaped in surprise. There, wagging its little paper tail, stood a paper dog.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421336426i/13360834.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>But at around the half-way mark, things just went downhill rapidly. Whilst I accepted that magic could be used to steal someone’s heart, I really hated the part of the book where Ceony got sucked into said heart, and had to battle her way through it! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And the romance was absolutely awful! She sees a few of his memories and suddenly she’s in love with him? Just what?<br><br><b><i>“He gestured to the empty expanse surrounding them. “This all of this. Why have you come so far to help me?””<br>“Because I think I’m falling in love with you,” She admitted.”</i></b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421336426i/13360835._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Really? Because you didn’t even like him at the start of the book.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I also noticed a bit of a ‘Wizard of Oz’ resemblance in this book. A girl sucked into a strange land through no fault of her own, complete with her little dog, and looking for someone called ‘Em’? Sounds like Dorothy to me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421336426i/13360836._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending of this was a relief, and I was so glad that the book ended at 96%! The last 20% of the book was just painful to get through. My eyes now need a rest from all the rolling they did.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421336426ra/13360837.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>4 out of 10<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2550677828" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2550677828" />
    <a title="Aisling Zena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18444439-aisling-zena"><img alt="Aisling Zena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385321518p2/18444439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2550677828?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aisling Zena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aisling Zena" href="/user/show/18444439-aisling-zena">Aisling Zena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2550677828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4606490548782351586"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I have a feeling I read this at the right time and mood. I quite enjoyed it. For me, a sign of a good fantasy book is it's ability to transport you. And this one certainly did that for me.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1538590192ra/26396190.gif' width='400' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I know that several of my GR friends couldn't get into this but I fell into it effortlessly. The setting is in the UK, in the early 1900s but magic exists. There's Smelters who bewitch metal, Polymorphs that manipulate Plastic, Gaffers who enchant glass and so on. Ceony has her heart set on being a Sm</span>
  <span id="freeText4606490548782351586" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br>I have a feeling I read this at the right time and mood. I quite enjoyed it. For me, a sign of a good fantasy book is it's ability to transport you. And this one certainly did that for me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1538590192ra/26396190.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I know that several of my GR friends couldn't get into this but I fell into it effortlessly. The setting is in the UK, in the early 1900s but magic exists. There's Smelters who bewitch metal, Polymorphs that manipulate Plastic, Gaffers who enchant glass and so on. Ceony has her heart set on being a Smelter but after all her hard work , at graduation time she is assigned to become a Folder. Folders enchant paper and they are going extinct as no one considers it a valuable magic to have. But Ceony has no choice, it's paper or nothing. Once one bonds with their material, they can never revert it. As she is coming to terms with her fate and the crash of her dreams, Ceony also begins her apprenticeship with her new mentor and teacher, Magician Emery Thane. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1538590192i/26396191._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>But it's not all paper hearts and roses and soon she learns not to underestimate what paper can do. When an Excisioner, a dark Magician controlling blood and flesh, decides to take her teacher's heart with her literally, Ceony is left with no choice but to try and save him.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1538591578ra/26396347.gif" width="400" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I found all the magic "powers" fascinating and truly unique. I think that's what held my interest throughout most of the book. I wanted to see what more could be done by what power. Ceony is quite a ballsy heroine, especially for it's era, yes she's immature, rash and a bit arrogant but that's how people in their late teens, early twenties often are. It didn't bother me in this book as it fits the situation. It's geared I think for more YA/NA audience. It has no sexy times and very minimal romance. But I was quite enthralled with all the world building regardless. <br><br>If you feel like a fantasy book, I'd recommend it purely for it's originality with the Folders and their magic. I found those parts the most fascinating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4606490548782351586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1079503243" />
    <a title="Wart Hill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4621717-wart-hill"><img alt="Wart Hill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456668366p2/4621717.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1079503243?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wart Hill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wart Hill" href="/user/show/4621717-wart-hill">Wart Hill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4621717-wart-hill?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4621717-wart-hill?shelf=arc2014">arc2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1079503243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9321531844253954014">You can read this and other reviews at <a href='http://thingsifindwhileshelving.tumblr.com/post/102611319161/arc-review-the-paper-magician-by-charlie-n-holmberg' rel='nofollow noopener'>Things I Find While Shelving</a><br/><br/><i>I received a free ARC Via Netgalley</i><br/><br/>BOOK you could’ve been five stars. You mostly deserved five stars. You were so good! Ceony, while talented and smart and possessing a photographic memory, wasn’t perfect. She didn’t get every fold right the first time. She didn’t take to being a folder right away, and she didn’t change her mind for no apparent reason. She changed her mind because Emery Thane, while different, is also super freak</span>
  <span id="freeText9321531844253954014" style="display:none">You can read this and other reviews at <a href="http://thingsifindwhileshelving.tumblr.com/post/102611319161/arc-review-the-paper-magician-by-charlie-n-holmberg" rel="nofollow noopener">Things I Find While Shelving</a><br /><br /><i>I received a free ARC Via Netgalley</i><br /><br />BOOK you could’ve been five stars. You mostly deserved five stars. You were so good! Ceony, while talented and smart and possessing a photographic memory, wasn’t perfect. She didn’t get every fold right the first time. She didn’t take to being a folder right away, and she didn’t change her mind for no apparent reason. She changed her mind because Emery Thane, while different, is also super freaking nice and he was the invisible hand behind her ability to get the education she wanted - though I don’t think he wanted her to know that.<br /><br />The showdown wasn’t flying spells. It was a struggle through a dying man’s heart, seeing his memories - good and bad. Fighting through his hopes and fears so she can get out and stop the woman who she’s fighting. A practitioner of dark magic, bonded to blood. Human blood. *shudder*.<br /><br />And in the end, all it takes is paper, words, and a strong voice to give Ceony the chance to get away, to get the heart back to its owner.<br /><br />To save a life.<br /><br />BOOK I FUCKING LOVED YOU.<br /><br />And then Ceony was ~falling in love~ with Emery Thane. Don’t buy it. Nope. Not for a second. Wasn’t necessary, came out of left field, and I get that romance sells but it just didn’t feel right. It felt like it was added for the sake of having some sort of romance. Their relationship never felt that way to me.<br /><br />So you lost a star. Sorry book.<br /><br />Looking forward to book two!</span>

<div id="review_2055319174" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2055319174?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="WhatIReallyRead" class="user" itemprop="url" name="WhatIReallyRead" href="/user/show/52500467-whatireallyread">WhatIReallyRead</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=comfort-read">comfort-read</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2055319174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1464732087810419328"><b>5 "exactly what I needed right now" stars.</b><br/><br/>The Paper Magician turned out to be a quick and delightful read. Set in 1901 London, it gave me a distinct magic-y feeling I love so much. The atmosphere reminded me of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294.Howl_s_Moving_Castle__Howl_s_Moving_Castle___1_' title='Howl's Moving Castle (Howl's Moving Castle, #1) by Diana Wynne Jones' rel='nofollow noopener'>Howl's Moving Castle</a> somehow.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1502914171ra/23610240.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It can easily be read as a standalone - the ending is well-rounded in a way that allows but does not require a sequel. <br/><br/>Even though the MCs are 19 and 30 years old, the book itself and the world depicted in it are a little naive, as if the book is meant for you</span>
  <span id="freeText1464732087810419328" style="display:none"><b>5 "exactly what I needed right now" stars.</b><br><br>The Paper Magician turned out to be a quick and delightful read. Set in 1901 London, it gave me a distinct magic-y feeling I love so much. The atmosphere reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294.Howl_s_Moving_Castle__Howl_s_Moving_Castle___1_" title="Howl's Moving Castle (Howl's Moving Castle, #1) by Diana Wynne Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">Howl's Moving Castle</a> somehow.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1502914171ra/23610240.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It can easily be read as a standalone - the ending is well-rounded in a way that allows but does not require a sequel. <br><br>Even though the MCs are 19 and 30 years old, the book itself and the world depicted in it are a little naive, as if the book is meant for younger audiences. It certainly didn't feel like any of the YA books I've ever read.<br><br>I liked both of the main characters: Ceony - a practical, no-nonsense sort, and Emery - a kind, intelligent and all-around good guy. <br><br><i>“But how will I know if he’s acting strange?” Ceony asked. “He’s strange already.”</i><br><br>In the beginning it surprised me a little that the school board would ship a 19-y.o. girl to become an apprentice and live with a 30-y.o. man, just the two of them in the same house. Isn't that, like, a little creepy? But it wasn't. <br><br>So now I'm off to the next one. Hopefully it will be just as enchanting.<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="1464732087810419328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17440418264850816046">This book came along at just the right time for me. I needed something light and magical, and this book did what I expected. I loved the magic system. It was different, and I think it worked well. I particularly liked Ceony, the main character. She was interesting and bold, and I particularly loved the relationship that she formed with the dog. I liked her independence, and the the way that she wasn't treated like a second class citizen, just because she is female. <br/>It isn't relevant, but the fro</span>
  <span id="freeText17440418264850816046" style="display:none">This book came along at just the right time for me. I needed something light and magical, and this book did what I expected. I loved the magic system. It was different, and I think it worked well. I particularly liked Ceony, the main character. She was interesting and bold, and I particularly loved the relationship that she formed with the dog. I liked her independence, and the the way that she wasn't treated like a second class citizen, just because she is female. <br />It isn't relevant, but the front cover is gorgeous. The design would be enough to encourage me to pick this one up. I have took two stars off this book as for one, the plot became rather dull halfway through reading, and I found I had to push through, which is never a good sign, and two, the romance. Without saying too much, I do think it was incredibly rushed, and I do wonder, whether it was actually necessary to include it at all? Time will tell! </span>

<div id="review_3226002987" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3226002987" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35799-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1250283102p2/35799.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3226002987?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/35799-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3226002987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1137025701493757259">This is a fun, light read. A good start for a series, I thought. I liked how magic was treated in this - each magician has to bond with his/her element and then that is the type of magic s/he does forever. Ceony, the main character, is an apprentice paper magician who is disappointed that she didn't get to choose her element (she wanted metal) but was placed with paper because of a lack of paper magicians. When her mentor is attacked, she has to save him, and she learns a lot about paper and all</span>
  <span id="freeText1137025701493757259" style="display:none">This is a fun, light read. A good start for a series, I thought. I liked how magic was treated in this - each magician has to bond with his/her element and then that is the type of magic s/he does forever. Ceony, the main character, is an apprentice paper magician who is disappointed that she didn't get to choose her element (she wanted metal) but was placed with paper because of a lack of paper magicians. When her mentor is attacked, she has to save him, and she learns a lot about paper and all it can do.<br /><br />I see a lot of reviewers complaining because the author used language they would not have used in the London of the time period. Well, you know what else they wouldn't have used during that time? MAGIC. It's fiction. It's set in an alternate universe. They have what they call "buggies" but apparently those have motors - one was also referred to as an automobile and one time, one was "left running". Complaints about the main character using current slang are off base. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1137025701493757259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2364286019" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2364286019?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sylvia Mercedes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sylvia Mercedes" href="/user/show/64427042-sylvia-mercedes">Sylvia Mercedes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=strong-female-characters">strong-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=slow-middle">slow-middle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=stayed-up-till-four-in-the-morning">stayed-up-till-four-in-the-morning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=all-about-the-heroes">all-about-the-heroes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2364286019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18198636303234590035">So, I DID like this one. I'm only giving it three stars because it was problematic in some ways. But once the action really hit, I was definitely caught up in the adventure! This was a late-into-the-night read for me because I couldn't stop turning those pages. The magic system was utterly unique and fascinating, and I loved watching the clever ways in which Ceony used her "useless" magic against such a formidable opponent. Epic!<br/><br/>Anyway, probably a <b>3.5</b> for me when all is said and done. It had it'</span>
  <span id="freeText18198636303234590035" style="display:none">So, I DID like this one. I'm only giving it three stars because it was problematic in some ways. But once the action really hit, I was definitely caught up in the adventure! This was a late-into-the-night read for me because I couldn't stop turning those pages. The magic system was utterly unique and fascinating, and I loved watching the clever ways in which Ceony used her "useless" magic against such a formidable opponent. Epic!<br /><br />Anyway, probably a <b>3.5</b> for me when all is said and done. It had it's problems, but it had plenty of virtues to balance those problems out, and I'm definitely curious to read the next book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18198636303234590035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2559731102" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2559731102" />
    <a title="Leigh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/81540896-leigh"><img alt="Leigh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536148599p2/81540896.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2559731102?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leigh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leigh" href="/user/show/81540896-leigh">Leigh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/81540896-leigh?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2559731102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7279871905771663270">This book is the first in a series; it is written in third person and is very easy to read. There is not any or very few cases of explicit language in this book. There are however several descriptions of body parts and blood, so if you are a bit squeamish, i wouldn't recommended this. But the book does have multiple flash backs - which I know some people do find off putting, I didn't mind then in this case as they moved the story along and helped me to understand the characters and world better.</span>
  <span id="freeText7279871905771663270" style="display:none">This book is the first in a series; it is written in third person and is very easy to read. There is not any or very few cases of explicit language in this book. There are however several descriptions of body parts and blood, so if you are a bit squeamish, i wouldn't recommended this. But the book does have multiple flash backs - which I know some people do find off putting, I didn't mind then in this case as they moved the story along and helped me to understand the characters and world better. This book is also a very short read I think, it's just over 200 pages and the pace of the story and the writing style means that is it quite possible to read it all in one setting.<br /><br />The book centres on Ceony Twill, who had just graduated from the Magical School, Tagis Praff. She is hoping to become an apprentice Smelter - a Metal Magician, now she has finished her studies, but is instead given the apprenticeship of being a Folder, a Paper Magician. We follow Ceony as she begins to learn the basics of being a Paper magician. Only for tragedy to strike when her teacher has his heart ripped out!<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book. I liked the magical system in place, it was well thought out and very unique, I had not encountered a system like this before. All man made items are able to be manipulated by magic and it was quite fascinating finding out some of the items that the magicians were able to make, such as paper snow which is cold to touch, paper pets and enchanted bullets. The world was interesting too, although there was little world building in the novel. I did still manage to get the feel of the 19th century from the novel, so perhaps, there is just enough. <br /><br />After reading some reviews on here about this book though, I think that criticisms of the novel’s setting and it not adhering to social conventions of the time, such as Ceony being allowed to live in a house with a single man, she is not related to, unjust. I personally, found it quite refreshing to read a book set in the 19th century which didn't treat woman as second class citizens and allowed them to be independent and work. I feel it added to the otherness of the world and just took it as a part of the world building; it also made the novel more enjoyable I think.<br /><br />My only criticism, is that the romance felt rather rushed and forced, but I won't get anymore into that as I don't want to spoil the book for anyone else.<br /><br />I am looking forward to read the next book and the rest in the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7279871905771663270" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1942320620" />
    <a title="Ova - Excuse My Reading" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5316099-ova---excuse-my-reading"><img alt="Ova - Excuse My Reading" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543876995p2/5316099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1942320620?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ova - Excuse My Reading" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ova - Excuse My Reading" href="/user/show/5316099-ova---excuse-my-reading">Ova - Excuse My Reading</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22521286-the-paper-magician">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1942320620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9726454236287882828">This was a short and sweet read, I like Ceony and would love to read more of her adventures!<br/><br/>I loved the way Paper Magic works, although there are lots of books about magic, Holmberg still was able to create an imaginative and original way in magical world.<br/><br/>My only criticism would be that the actions developed a bit too quickly, but this seems like a trait in YA fiction so I am bypassing this and giving this book a 4 stars for the nice company. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mSFIlaoXH6tfqsCusOTe66AYFVGj5JU9xMGUIM8zoCPwrQIwSKe90QKOETtFl/ZslziF5utpV7VQH7u1kVTMsg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ASZzIkXLqP7UwS0t2nTBfJTyNw2zYzrl80hDBb0Q7YloqjmHp3sKhInl/LgvB+n7o9Knuvvu+G1nlmyQ43eBGA==')})
  }
